The Ministry of Foreign Affairs Sends Personnel to Investigate Nanyang Commerce

Chen Chunpu and Others Are Scheduled to Sail on March 5th

Wu Zhihao's Views on Promoting Domestic Goods

According to the Shiye News Agency, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, in order to promote trade in domestic goods in Nanyang and improve the lives of overseas Chinese, has specially commissioned Chen Chunpu, Liang Yugao, Zheng Lin, and others to go to Nanyang for investigation, in order to facilitate progress. After receiving the order, Chen Chunpu and others are scheduled to leave Shanghai on March 5th and sail abroad. Therefore, they sent a letter to Mr. Wu Zhihao, Standing Committee Member of the China National Products Production and Sales United Company, a few days ago, soliciting opinions from domestic goods manufacturers on promoting domestic goods in Nanyang for reference. The letter and Mr. Wu's opinions are excerpted below:

Chen Chunpu and Others Were Ordered to Investigate: The letter from Chen Chunpu and others to Wu Zhihao reads, "Respectfully, Chunpu and others have been dispatched by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to Nanyang to investigate commercial affairs, inspect the affairs of consulates, and matters related to overseas Chinese. We will leave Shanghai on March 5th and sail abroad. Before leaving the country, we intend to collect opinions from domestic goods manufacturers on promoting domestic goods in Nanyang for reference, so that when we arrive in various parts of Nanyang, we can discuss solutions with consuls, chambers of commerce, and overseas Chinese merchants, and report the research and investigation results to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs as a basis for implementation and promotion. We respectfully ask you to convey this intention to the manufacturers, and we kindly ask you to collect the opinions of the manufacturers first and transfer them through your company. We will be grateful. Sincerely, Chen Chunpu, Liang Yugao, Zheng Lin, investigators of Nanyang commercial affairs dispatched by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs."

Mr. Wu's Reply Expressing His Opinion: After receiving the letter, Mr. Wu drafted six points of opinion in reply as follows: "Respectfully, I have received your letter and am delighted to learn that you are going to Nanyang to investigate commercial affairs on a mission from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and inspect the affairs of the consulates. I hope that you will work hard in a foreign land and benefit the overseas Chinese. I am honored to hear this from afar and will not delay in my admiration. I am entrusted to collect opinions from domestic goods manufacturers on promoting domestic goods in Nanyang. In addition to forwarding this to the manufacturers as directed, I will draft opinions in the coming days and submit them to you through our company for reference. I would also like to briefly state my humble opinions for your selection. I believe that if we want to open up the Nanyang market today in order to build a solid foundation for the foreign trade of domestic goods, although the details are many and the fundamentals are different, we must not be biased. However, after weighing the importance and considering the urgency, the following matters are the most pressing needs of our domestic goods industry at present: (1) The establishment of commercial officers. Since the last century, international trade has become increasingly prosperous, and consulates in various countries have established commercial officers to understand local needs and study the psychology of residents, in order to develop trade in their own countries. Looking back at the places where our domestic products are sold abroad, the ports of Nanyang have always been the most prosperous. Six million of our overseas Chinese pioneers have been operating there. Although our government has established consulates in various Nanyang ports for diplomatic governance, it is still difficult to take into account the promotion of domestic goods due to the limited number of personnel and the complexity of affairs. If our domestic goods industry wants to develop in the Nanyang markets in the future, it is necessary to imitate the establishment of commercial officers with special responsibilities. (2) The opening of domestic goods exhibition halls. Although our domestic goods industry has indeed made progress day by day, we feel a lack of foreign exhibitions and publicity. The overseas Chinese in Nanyang have always been known for their enthusiasm for patriotism. However, being far away overseas, they often feel isolated from the industrial and commercial situation of the motherland, and domestic industries are even more unclear. Even if our overseas Chinese are eager to be patriotic, at a time when various countries are implementing commercial control policies, how can they not be disappointed in the motherland and be bewitched by foreign goods? Moreover, the Nanyang scholars do not have a sense of nationality among the various countries. Whoever's publicity is more effective, they will be their customers. The way of publicity should not be ignored. The so-called establishment of exhibition halls today is to collect domestic products for exhibition and use the publicity of real objects to encourage our overseas Chinese and local natives to use our domestic goods through continuous observation. The benefits to the promotion of domestic goods should not be insignificant. (3) The organization of domestic goods promotion agencies. The decline in trade in various parts of Nanyang has been caused by the exclusion of certain foreigners, which cannot be denied. However, the lack of adequate communication between producers and sellers is also a major reason. Since there is no specific organization to promote domestic goods in various parts of Nanyang, domestic factories are often hesitant and hesitant to move forward. Overseas Chinese in various parts of Nanyang also find it difficult to unify the steps of promotion due to the scattered transport of domestic goods to the south. Therefore, both in terms of main force and effectiveness, it is not enough to compete with the Japanese's planned trade. If we want to make up for this defect, we must unite the forces and jointly organize a large-scale domestic goods promotion agency in various ports of Nanyang. Our company can do its best in terms of its responsibilities. (4) The establishment of banks. There are many overseas Chinese in various parts of Nanyang, but it is not easy to find banks created by the Chinese themselves. This lacks the connection between fingers and arms in the development of the domestic goods industry. It is indeed difficult in practice to make the fragile domestic goods forces and maneuver in the field of international commercial warfare. If we want to develop trade in various parts of Nanyang, we should set up national banks and commercial banks in important areas of Nanyang, specializing in supporting the domestic goods industry as their business, and handling various types of mortgage remittance, exchange, and loan issuance. This can make both producers and sellers develop due to the proper financial adjustment. (5) The establishment of shipping. Transportation is a powerful tool for the smooth flow of goods. The reason why the relationship between supply and demand in today's society is so frequent is due to the development of transportation. Most of the goods transported from our country to Nanyang rely on foreign ships as their intermediaries. This not only results in a huge outflow of national funds, but also often involves unnecessary waste and trouble in terms of time and procedures. Because foreign ships always treat goods differently based on whether they are domestic or foreign. If they are domestic goods, they are given priority. If they are our country's goods, they are charged heavy freight. Nothing is more unfair than this. With the vast territory and abundant resources of our country, if we do not strive to reduce transportation costs, simplify procedures, and save time, domestic factories will be hesitant to move forward due to the cumbersome and heavy relationships. Water and land transportation has been implemented in various parts of our country. If the Ministry of Communications can have commercial ships sailing directly to Nanyang, whether it is in the border area or the interior, it can become more and more active due to the convenience of combined transportation. This is a great help in encouraging the foreign trade of domestic goods. As for plugging leaks, it is especially a matter of the future. (6) The holding of mutual inspections. Military tactics say, 'Know yourself and your enemy, and you will win every battle.' If we want to develop Nanyang, we must first have a comprehensive understanding of Nanyang society in order to deeply understand where Nanyang needs are and adapt to them. Therefore, we must unite domestic industrial and commercial leaders and industrial officials to conduct on-site inspections, either annually or every other year, so that our country's goods industry can have adequate guidance for exporting to Nanyang. As for the recent developments in our country's goods industry, in order to make Nanyang people aware of them, we should also invite Nanyang overseas Chinese organizations to continuously return to the country for inspection, so as to exchange perspectives and achieve the effect of mutual assistance. The above is only a discussion of the most important issues. As for the steps of implementation and methods, they all require you to discuss with local overseas Chinese organizations and research with local leaders, and make suggestions to the government for clear decision-making. I hope you will correct my humble opinions. Sincerely, Wu Zhihao to Mr. Chen Chunpu, Jie Yugao, Zheng Lin."

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce Officially Denies Sending a Special Envoy to Japan

The Chairman of the Association Made a Special Statement Yesterday

All Aspects of the Japanese Telegram Are Considered Inaccurate

According to the China News Agency, regarding the news reported in the Japanese telegram yesterday that the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce had sent a representative to negotiate on Sino-Japanese economic cooperation, the China News Agency reporter interviewed Mr. Lin Kanghou, chairman of the association, at the Bankers Association yesterday. Mr. Lin absolutely denied all aspects of the news reported in the Japanese telegram. His statement is recorded below:

The News Reported in the Japanese Telegram: According to Mr. Lin, the Japanese telegram reported that the association had sent Jin Bofan, general manager of the International Enterprise Company, as an envoy to Japan to investigate concrete plans for Sino-Japanese cooperation, in order to express each other's sincerity and create materials for establishing a cooperation plan. The telegram also reported that Mr. Jin made a statement saying that the general industrial and commercial circles in China generally welcomed Japanese goods. After investigation, the association did not send this so-called special envoy to Japan. The manager of the International Enterprise Company is Chen Bofan, not Jin Bofan. Mr. Chen is an overseas Chinese who often resides in Kobe or Shanghai.

Absolutely Denies: Although the person is acquainted with me, he is not a special envoy sent by the Federation of Chambers of Commerce. However, before Mr. Chen went to Japan this time, there was a private contact. The industrial and commercial circles of our country wanted to know the inside story of the Sino-Japanese economic cooperation plan reported by the Japanese side. I also knew Mr. Hengzhu, the Japanese commercial officer who published this plan, so I introduced Chen to him and asked him to inquire about the truth on his behalf. As for Mr. Chen's statement in Japan that the industrial and commercial circles of our country welcomed Japanese goods, it is clear that the Japanese side is using this to promote themselves. Our country's industry and commerce do not welcome the import of any foreign goods.

Shen Xin Company Sends Personnel to Japan for Investigation

Mr. Hui and Mr. Zou Departed for Japan Yesterday

Silk Industry Magnate Xue Shou Xuan Sailed Abroad Yesterday

Investigating the Silk Industries of European and American Countries for Reference

Xue Shou Xuan, a magnate in the silk industry in Wuxi, in view of the declining silk industry in our country and the lack of exports, has specially gone to Europe and the United States to investigate the silk industry. He came to Shanghai from Wuxi the day before yesterday and took the President Coolidge to the United States at 11:00 yesterday morning. According to Mr. Xue's statement to the Shen Shi News Agency reporter before his departure, Wuxi is the center of the silk industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, and it controls the hub of the national silk industry. In recent years, silk exports have declined sharply, and the silk industry in Wuxi has suffered a setback. Silk factories have closed one after another, and the silkworm seed industry has also been greatly affected. The reasons for the sluggish silk exports are nothing more than poor quality and Japanese silk occupying our market. This time, he is going abroad to investigate the silk industry in the United States, France, Germany, Japan, and other countries, so that after returning to China, he can develop our silk industry for reference. The investigation period is set for eight months, and he is expected to return to China in November of this year.

Match Tycoons from China, Japan, and the United States Will Hold a Ceasefire Conference

Liu Hongsheng, Takikawa, and Others Will Gather in Shanghai Soon

Our Government Authorities Will Also Attend

According to the Hua Dong News Agency, in recent years, the match industry in our country has been quite vigorous, but because there are too many manufacturers, the goods produced are oversupplied. Recently, the Japanese government has decided to dump a large number of matches in China in order to maintain the survival of Japanese match factories and the livelihood of countless Japanese match workers. Our country's match manufacturers already feel that the domestic factories are oversupplied. If Japanese matches are dumped again, our side will inevitably fight back, and the domestic match industry will decline further. At the same time, the only American match company in China, the American Guang Match Company, has also been affected by our country's match industry, and sales have been sluggish. It intends to cooperate with our country. Therefore, the match manufacturers of the three countries have held a ceasefire cooperation meeting in Shanghai. According to the Hua Dong News Agency reporter's investigation yesterday morning, this matter can be realized in the near future. Our country's match manufacturers have been holding meetings for days and have thoroughly explored this matter. Recently, our side plans to send personnel to Japan to visit Mr. Takikawa, the match king of Japan, to discuss the implementation plan, and then invite Mr. Takikawa to Shanghai to discuss the ceasefire of matches and the production and sales cooperation of matches in the three countries with Mr. Liu Hongsheng, the match tycoon of South China, Mr. Zhang Xinwu, the match tycoon of North China, and the general manager of the American Guang Match Company, a match tycoon of American merchants in China. Since this matter is of great importance, our government authorities may send personnel from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Industry to attend. According to relevant people in the match manufacturing industry in this city, the implementation of this measure can prevent the match manufacturers of the three countries from perishing together and can maintain their survival.

The General Association of Marine Engineers Submits a Petition to the Ministry for Relief of Unemployed Seafarers

Listing Eight Conditions of Request

Submitting this petition due to prolonged unemployment and lack of means of livelihood, electing representatives to present the petition. It is observed that China's maritime rights have been seized by others, the shipping industry is in decline, and the loss of rights is enormous. In recent years, the government has emphasized the shipping industry, established maritime administration agencies, and managed painstakingly with great effort. Indeed, this matter is of great importance, with thousands of threads to untangle, relating to national rights above and people's livelihoods below. It is appropriate to coordinate the overall situation and consider all parties, first determining the fundamental principles, and then proceeding step by step, in an orderly manner, to fully implement and maximize benefits, achieving the ultimate goal. Therefore, the legal system and decrees related to maritime administration, as well as various aspects of improvement and elimination, should be treated with absolute seriousness, to avoid any inappropriateness that leads to the phenomenon of square pegs in round holes, causing the pain of cutting one's feet to fit the shoes for the Chinese people. Currently, members of our association are affected by the encroachment of unlicensed marine engineers on their occupations, resulting in the unemployment of many, prolonged idleness, and unbearable hardship. We will explain the details and respectfully submit them to your ministry. According to international practice, ships of a country are generally staffed by nationals as navigation, marine engineering, and crew members, and foreigners are not allowed to be employed. Chinese merchants, bound by prejudice, often prefer to employ foreign crew members who enjoy extraterritorial rights, colluding with each other for mutual benefit, creating an unprecedented evil precedent in the world. The government has never strictly cracked down on this, allowing them to encroach on the occupations of Chinese people. For decades, this has become a situation that is too large to control. On the one hand, the government has conducted examinations for Chinese crew members, especially since June of the 22nd year (of the Republic), when Xu Zufan, as the chairman of the examination committee, initiated the practice of implementing examinations for crew members applying for certificates. After this, the service standards for crew members should be based on the existence or absence of certificates. Unexpectedly, there are still many who do not have certificates but are still employed. This not only has no solution for foreign crew members encroaching on occupations, but also has no solution for illegal Chinese crew members. The value of certificates is equal to zero, which is why the number of unemployed members of the association is increasing. Furthermore, according to the certificate regulations, crew members are not allowed to hold positions beyond the scope of the duties listed on their certificates. Your ministry had decided to ban this by the end of last year. The association fully expected this to be implemented at that time, giving the crew member community a chance to refresh itself. However, before the deadline, your ministry issued Instruction No. 6358 on December 15th, extending the deadline for another six months. The only reason given was that many crew members had difficulty coming to the ministry for examinations due to ship voyages, and this was done out of consideration for the situation below. Upon investigation, over-ranked crew members are those currently holding positions. Lowering their rank, at most, would be like changing a chief engineer to a first engineer, decreasing in succession. It would not result in unemployment. Your ministry should know that the situations of over-ranked crew members and unemployed crew members are vastly different. If it is truly out of consideration, then you should not only consider over-ranked crew members but also forget about unemployed crew members with certificates. You should differentiate between urgent and less urgent matters and handle them impartially. Because over-ranked employment is fundamentally illegal, now, instead of banning it, you are showing consideration, which, although nominally an extension, is actually an endorsement, adding another layer of protection to their illegal behavior. Therefore, according to the current method, the glimmer of hope that unemployed crew members have had for the past six months has been completely extinguished. Moreover, the extension will inevitably lead to malpractices, namely, shipowners taking advantage of loopholes, often making excuses to avoid employing formal crew members, precisely because they are taking advantage of their illegality, to recruit them at lower wages, clearly reducing expenses through illegal means. Your ministry had already issued Instruction No. 2789 on this situation in October of the 21st year, fully understanding the crux of the matter. Why is there a discrepancy between the past and the present, which is perplexing? (Omission) Some members of the association have been idle for as long as one or two years. Although we sent a letter to the Shanghai Maritime Administration Bureau last year requesting them to handle unemployment registration, hoping they could find ways to place them, no one has been placed to this day, and the number of unemployed people continues to increase. After discussion at a meeting, it was decided that the situation was serious, and it was decided to nominate representatives to present a written petition. The conditions of the request are: (1) Please promptly issue a ministerial order to all competent maritime administration agencies, stating that from the date of the order, anyone who has not obtained a crew member certificate is not allowed to be employed in any position. Those who are already on board and whose employment began before the date of the ministerial order, and who have previously applied for employment registration with the Maritime Administration Bureau and obtained a seaman's manual stating the fact, shall be temporarily allowed to serve, but the shipping company shall be instructed to notify them to apply for examination within one month, or within two arrivals of their serving vessel at the port of Shanghai, and those who exceed the deadline shall be ordered to retire. (2) Crew members applying for examination shall be required to report for examination within one month, or within two arrivals of their serving vessel at the port of Shanghai, after receiving the approval from the ministry to go to the ministry for examination. Those who evade the deadline or fail to complete the examination shall be banned from serving. (3) Crew members engaged in examination shall be allowed to find qualified personnel to act on their behalf for the positions they left behind, and shall be allowed to retain their original positions. Those who pass the examination and are able to obtain certificates equivalent to their original positions shall be guaranteed reinstatement, and shipping companies shall not refuse. (4) Crew members who fail the current examination and are issued lower-level certificates shall not be allowed to serve beyond their level. (5) Those who serve beyond two levels shall be ordered to cease serving, and their existing qualifications shall only be calculated according to the level of the certificate they hold. (6) Crew members applying for examination who are willing to take a written test shall be allowed to choose the type of examination, regardless of Category A or B. Since they have undergone examination, their grades should be used to determine their ranking, and there should be no preconceived notions, using merchant marine schools as the standard for determining levels. The maritime profession is shared by all seafarers and should not be monopolized by one system or faction. Therefore, the regulation that those who do not come from merchant marine schools shall not be issued Category A certificates should be abolished to promote fairness. (7) The Shanghai Maritime Administration Bureau's handling of crew member registration is improper, and there are complaints from the outside world. Those with verifiable facts, such as chief engineers serving without certificates, impersonating others, and not applying for examinations without certificates, who do not meet the statutory qualifications, are not noticed by the bureau. It is not known why this is the case. Therefore, as a thorough solution, all matters related to the employment, dismissal, and change of serving vessels of marine engineers in Shanghai should be determined to be handled by the association on behalf of the applicant, so as to supervise each other and provide relief. (8) The provisions of Articles 8 and 9 of the Implementing Rules of the Provisional Regulations for Crew Member Examination shall be amended. They stipulate that chief engineers who hold certificates must continue to serve for more than five years before they can be exempted from examining other marine engineers, and other marine engineers must hold the positions stated on their certificates for more than one year before they are allowed to undergo original-level examinations. At present, foreign crew members and illegal Chinese crew members are not prohibited and are still allowed to serve, clearly infringing on the rights of crew members who have already obtained certificates. The government is not only unable to protect them, but also imposes harsh restrictions on them. Therefore, for the sake of unemployed crew members, they have already felt the pain of life, and after several years, even if they do not fill the trenches or die from cold and hunger, their original qualifications will have already disappeared and they will no longer have the opportunity to serve as crew members. This is a suicidal policy and should be abolished. The above eight items, in light of the current situation, are sufficient to show that the cause of crew member unemployment is not due to a natural trend, but rather to the failure of maritime administration to seize the opportunity. Therefore, the order allowing over-ranked employment is a step towards disaster, and it must not be extended again after the deadline. We believe that your ministry is in charge of transportation, and if you do not resolve the issue of crew member unemployment as soon as possible, hidden dangers will lie dormant, and once they erupt, the promotion of China's shipping industry in the future may not be immune to its constraints. Looking to the future, we are particularly fearful. Therefore, in accordance with the discussion and decision method, together with the roster of unemployed members, we have prepared a written petition and personally ask that your Excellency accept the situation below and grant the requested items to be implemented as soon as possible, so as to provide relief and demonstrate assistance. We respectfully submit this to the Ministry of Transportation, earnestly hoping for your approval and compliance.

Shanghai Municipal Council's This Year's Public Works Construction Plan

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Public Works Department's work plan for this year, after having its budget for temporary expenses and recurrent expenses drafted, and classified according to urgency, was reviewed by the Public Works Committee and then submitted to the Finance Committee for review and decision. The main points are described below:

Bridge and Waterway Expenses: The completion expenses for the Liping Road and Dinghai Road bridges, after a reduction, are listed as 17,000 yuan. The expenses for repairing the riverbanks in various places have been reduced to 30,000 yuan. The extension expenses for the urgently needed sewers in the eastern district are 130,000 yuan. The construction expenses for sewage pipes, after a reduction in the settling pond item, are listed as 436,000 yuan. The Huishan wooden wharf is to be rebuilt into concrete for 40,000 yuan. The above are all considered urgent and are approved for expenditure.

Public Building Expenses: It is proposed to allocate 150,000 yuan for the construction of a passenger wharf on the Bund. The outstanding construction funds for the Public Works Branch on Tongzhou Road have been reduced to 20,000 yuan. The factory on Wuzhou Road is to be equipped with additional safety devices, listed as 7,500 yuan. The Antong Road branch is to build a storage shed and office for 15,000 yuan. Additional public toilets are to be built in various places where they are urgently needed for 15,000 yuan.

Park Equipment Expenses: 6,500 yuan is to be spent on rebuilding staff housing in Zhaofeng Park. 4,000 yuan is to be spent on the construction of a marble kiosk. 3,000 yuan is to be spent on adding public toilets. 11,000 yuan is to be spent on building two grandstands in Jiaozhou Park. 10,000 yuan is to be spent on a cool pavilion, drinking pool, and toilet. 6,000 yuan is to be spent on rebuilding a pavilion in the Bund Park. 3,000 yuan is to be spent on adding a toilet in Hongkou Park.

Road Project Expenses: The land acquisition expenses for road expansion and extension are listed as 1,500,000 yuan. The road construction expenses are listed as 700,000 yuan. According to the Director of Finance, the above temporary expenses are estimated based on the situation this year. In the event of financial difficulties, all but the absolutely necessary will inevitably be postponed.

Recurrent Expense Budget: The Public Works Department's recurrent expenses for 1935, including staff salaries, housing, road, waterway, and ditch management and maintenance expenses, garbage collection and disposal expenses, road lighting expenses, park maintenance and management expenses, etc., total 5,762,400 yuan. The previous year's budget was 5,734,500 yuan. All the numbers in each item may still be subject to appropriate amendments by the Finance Department and the Public Works Department before the final decision.

Xingye Trust Society Continues to Build Urban Housing

Styles are Divided into Types A and B

Sales Price Can be Paid in Installments

Since the central urban area has been actively developed by the municipal government and all sectors, it is now splendidly complete, and public buildings will also be completed one after another. In order to prosper the central urban area and meet the needs, the Shanghai Xingye Trust Society built dozens of houses between Minfu Road and Shiguang Road last year, which were sold in installments and were very popular among people from all walks of life. They were sold out soon. Last winter, the society added a small vegetable market and urban houses for rent, and opened small-scale department stores and daily necessities stores, which were even more convenient for the residents. Now, the society is building a second batch of two types of houses between Zhayin Road and Minfu Road in the central urban area. Type A occupies an area of about 1.5 mu, and Type B occupies about 1 mu. The houses are newly and thoughtfully designed, sturdily and beautifully built, and equipped with complete water, electricity, and sanitation facilities. There is space left outside the house for planting flowers and trees, surrounded by bamboo fences, which are elegant and unique. The sales price is low. Type A is 20,000 yuan per house, and Type B is 16,000 yuan, and it can be paid in installments. Construction began in December last year and will be completed by the end of July this year. The society has a simple brochure with detailed information on the style, size, and dimensions of the houses, as well as installment payment tables, for people from all walks of life to request.

All Severely Punished Separately

Two Criminals Detained for Other Cases

(3) Hua Detective Ji Cunyi, Hua Detectives Cui Chengke and Pang Yutang of the Chengdu Road Police Station, arrested the housewife Zhao Gu's, gamblers Sun Xiaobao, Chen Fusheng, Qiu Shengtang, women Zhang Wang's, Wang Zhu's, Chen Fang's, Wang Liu's, Yu Xu's, Shi Chen's, etc., a total of 29 people, and confiscated gambling equipment and gambling money, in Yongqingfang No. 35, Xinda Gu Road. (4) Hua Detective Zhou Mingshan and Ma Guangqi of the General Patrol Police Station, arrested gamblers Yang Qijie, Lu Gengsheng, Cai A'fu, Wang Su's, Lü Li's, etc., a total of 25 people, at No. 346 to 348 Edward Road. Yesterday morning, all the criminals were sentenced by the First Special District Court. However, Zhu A'mao, one of the gamblers arrested in Dadong, was arrested by the Xinza Police Station in the first year of the Republic for a case and then escaped from prison. Another person, Cao Changxing, was also detained for another case. Therefore, Judge Zhan Liangce ordered them to be returned to prison for the police to investigate and verify.

Young American House Servant Commits Suicide

The Meaning of Eight Characters in the Suicide Note is Unclear

Chen Shiming, a young man from Yangzhou, 18 years old, was introduced to work as a house servant at the residence of an American named Ross (transliteration) in room 31 of the Gao Ta Apartment, No. 1333 Xiafei Road, French Concession, last August, with a monthly salary of 10 yuan. His father, Chen Lihai, 43 years old, is currently working in a brothel in Tianjin. His mother, Chen Cui's, 37 years old, is currently working as an amah in a Westerner's house at No. 1590 Xiafei Road. At 10:30 AM yesterday morning, Shiming, alone in his employer Ross's room, for some unknown reason, suddenly had the idea of committing suicide. He first wrote a note with a pencil on a piece of paper, and then opened the cupboard and took out a six-round large-caliber revolver that his employer had prepared. Standing in front of the cupboard, he fired at his chest. The bullet pierced his chest and exited from his back, also shattering the glass of the dressing mirror placed against the wall behind him, also creating a hole. After being injured, Shiming fell to the ground and died. The other servants, Zhu Ziwen (30 years old, from Yangzhou) and the wet nurse, Udu Wengu (transliteration, 32-year-old Russian woman), heard the sound and entered the room to check. The deceased's body was covered in blood, flowing from the wound. They were greatly frightened and immediately called the employer, American Ross, to come and report to the French police, who sent Chinese and Western detectives to investigate. A piece of paper was found on a small table next to the body, with eight characters written on it ("字肝字精、不關傍人"), the meaning of which was unclear. They immediately took photos and moved the body to the Tongren Fuyuan branch of the mortuary for examination, waiting for a report to the Second Special District Court today to send personnel to examine it. The deceased's mother, Chen Cui's, received the news and rushed to the mortuary, weeping over the body. She also claimed that her son often joked with his fellow servants, such as the head servant, and that he must have been playing with the gun and accidentally shot himself, and asked the police to investigate.

A Record of the Opening of the Trial of the Hua Zhongchu Case of a Spring Dream of Victory, Generosity, and Heroism

The Audience Seats Were Filled With Prostitutes

Hua et al. Admitted to All Accusations

—The Two Prostitutes Each Paid 500 Yuan Deposit, the Rest Were Returned to Prison—

Hua Zhongchu, Ding Chengfu, Pan Ruilin, and Zhu Minggui, trainees at the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank on Henan Road, jointly exchanged 30,000 yuan of banknotes with blank paper and 12,305 yuan of ten-yuan banknotes with five-yuan banknotes. Hua also absconded to Hong Kong with the prostitutes Lao Er (Yan Caizhen) and Lao San (Wu Zhihua) from the Yinghong brothel in Huile Lane. The police successively captured and escorted them to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. This has been reported in detail in this newspaper. Longzhang Paper Mill's Machine Transformation a Great Success

Benefiting Culture and Saving Outflow of Capital

The Longzhang Machine Paper Mill on Longhua Road in Shanghai was established in the twenty-ninth year of the Guangxu reign of the former Qing Dynasty, and has been in operation for thirty years. Initially, it was a joint venture between the government and merchants, equipped with two American thin paper long-net paper-making machines. Japanese engineers and all important technical personnel were hired. Due to mismanagement, it suffered significant losses and was once suspended. Subsequently, Pang Laichen, a wealthy merchant from Nanxun, took over and transformed it into a commercial enterprise. He dismissed the Japanese personnel and reduced expenses. Since then, the operation has been smooth.

The factory has historically specialized in producing various types of "Yanglian Shi" (foreign stationery), which were popular throughout the country. After the September 18th Incident, the Northeast was lost, and sales were greatly affected, decreasing by about one-third each year. The current General Manager, Zhang Rangzhi, recognizing this situation, focused on also manufacturing foreign paper to prevent the overproduction of "Yanglian Shi" and to benefit the cultural industry significantly. The foreign paper used by the domestic printing industry was mostly imported, resulting in a huge outflow of capital each year. Paper manufacturers should take responsibility for reversing this trend. Therefore, an engineer was hired to the factory to try making "Daolin" (woodfree) paper, but the results were not entirely satisfactory. A Shanghai foreign firm was then requested to design and transform the paper-making machine to achieve the goal. The foreign firm drew up plans for transforming the machine, asking for more than ten thousand yuan, but the price was not agreed upon, so it was temporarily abandoned.

Subsequently, in May of last year (1934), Xue Liufeng, Zhang Linquan, Mu Shisong, Liu Zhenhua, etc., were hired to the factory to design and prototype. Starting in November, one part of the paper-making machine was dismantled and reassembled. On February 20th of this year, it began operating, and the results of trial production of gray wrapping paper and Mao Yuen (month calendar) paper were excellent. The factory owner, Pang Laichen, personally inspected the factory the next day and expressed great satisfaction. The transformation of the paper-making machine, the addition of machine parts, and labor and materials cost a total of more than ten thousand yuan, only one-tenth of the price quoted by the foreign firm. The cost was minimal, and the success was great. Even better, after the transformation, the machine can still produce "Yanglian Shi," maintaining the original purpose of the factory.

It is believed that this factory is the first in the country to independently design and install machines to manufacture foreign paper. Who says that China has no talent? Compared to Westerners, it is even better. The factory is currently preparing to produce various weights of Daolin paper, kraft paper, and colored cover paper samples to be distributed to major bookstores and printing factories in the country, requesting criticism and encouraging the use of domestic products to stem the outflow of capital. They also plan to establish a chemical testing laboratory to study foreign paper to meet social needs.

Public Works Department Upgrades Fire Hydrants

New Hydrants with Three Outlets

One Hydrant Installed Every 250 Feet

The Director of the Fire Department of the Public Works Department recently agreed with the Water Company to quickly upgrade the old-style hydrants on the streets, which only have one outlet, to new-style hydrants with three outlets. A total of 150 hydrants should be upgraded and installed each year so that there will be one new-style hydrant every 250 feet of road surface, and two hydrants at intersections. The supply and installation of these hydrants will be the responsibility of the company, and the ongoing maintenance costs, estimated at 70,000 yuan per year, will still be borne by the Public Works Department.

It has also been found that 1,038 private fire-fighting facilities are connected to the company's water pipes. The owners are responsible for the timely repair and painting. The Public Works Department has now decided that the Fire Department will strictly inspect them. The company and the owners will directly handle the repairs and costs.

Enthusiastic Response to Wanyou Wenku (Complete Library) Subscribers

Exceeding the Original Print Run of the First Phase

The second collection of Wanyou Wenku, published by the Commercial Press, ended its subscription period at the end of 1934. In addition to orders from libraries, schools, and individuals from all over the country, the education departments of Anhui, Zhejiang, Guangxi, Hunan, Sichuan, Fujian, Shandong, and other provinces have also ordered dozens to one or two hundred copies. The original print run of the books has already been nearly exhausted. Subsequently, in response to requests from various parties, a new installment payment and group sales subscription method was established on February 1, 1935. Purchasers can weigh their needs and urgency, or pay in installments, or select and purchase in groups according to their preferences, which is very convenient. Since the announcement of this method, new subscribers have been very enthusiastic. It is estimated that the books in the first phase, which will be published in March, will not be sufficient to meet demand. If reservations are made later, it will take two months to receive the books when the first edition is sold out. Those who order according to the new method should do so as early as possible. It is also heard that there are preferential methods for ordering the second collection of Wanyou Wenku if the first collection is also ordered at the same time.

Jailed for Buying a Diamond Ring

Yin Cunfu Sues the Wife of a Deceased Friend

Kuang Cheng, the second daughter-in-law of Kuang Zhongmou, a wealthy Wuxi merchant and owner of the Cheng Huang Miao market in this city (also known as Cheng Meifang), was once involved in a lawsuit in the Second Special District Court for colluding with her mother, Cheng Xu, to defraud Yin Cunfu of two diamond rings worth a significant amount. Cheng Xu was found guilty and sentenced to two years in prison. Kuang Cheng Meifang failed to appear in court, and the case was suspended.

The cause of this case is as follows: Yin Cunfu, a resident of No. 4 Xilin Hou Road, Ximenwai, has been engaged in real estate for many years. His business has been smooth, and he has accumulated a lot of wealth. In November of last year, Cheng Xu, a widow from Shanghai residing at No. 20 Dahua Lane, Nanyang Bridge in the French Concession, went to Yin Cunfu's house with her daughter, Kuang Cheng Meifang, and purchased two diamond rings from Yin, agreeing to a price of 2,900 yuan. She paid 1,000 yuan, leaving 1,900 yuan unpaid. Subsequently, the mother and daughter disappeared. Yin Cunfu, in desperation, hired a lawyer to sue Cheng Xu and Cheng Meifang in the Second Special District Court for fraud. As a result, Cheng Xu was sentenced to two years in prison. The second defendant, Kuang Cheng Meifang, was under the jurisdiction of Nanshi, so the plaintiff was ordered to file a separate lawsuit with the Nanshi District Court according to the law.

After receiving the complaint, the court ordered the accused to be interrogated. However, Kuang Cheng Meifang refused to appear in court, and the prosecutor filed a public prosecution. Yesterday morning at 10 a.m., Judge Chen Jingze specially opened the 13th courtroom for trial. The plaintiff, Yin Cunfu, and his private prosecution agent lawyer appeared in court. The first defendant, Cheng Xu, had previously been transferred from the Second Special District Court and detained. The judge ascended the bench and ordered the plaintiff, Yin Cunfu, to the dock.

After hearing the testimony, he said, "I am 44 years old. Last winter, in November, Cheng Xu came to my house with her daughter, Kuang Cheng Meifang, to buy diamond rings."

The judge asked, "How did they know you had these diamond rings at home?"

He replied, "Cheng Xu's husband was a friend of mine when he was alive, and we had a good relationship, so they knew."

The judge asked, "How many diamond rings did they buy?"

He replied, "In early November, Cheng Xu came to my house alone and bought a diamond ring for 1,600 yuan. About ten days later, Cheng Xu came to my house again with her daughter, Cheng Meifang, but I was out on business and didn't see them. Soon after, the mother and daughter came again, but I still didn't see them. The last time was on November 19th, when I finally met them. At that time, Cheng Xu paid 1,000 yuan, and Kuang Cheng Meifang bought another diamond ring from me. I thought she was the daughter-in-law of a wealthy merchant and had no other concerns, so I let her take it. Later, I learned that they had pawned it for cash."

The judge asked, "Then the pawn ticket was returned to you?"

He replied, "The pawn ticket was only returned to my house yesterday."

The judge asked, "How much was it pawned for?"

He replied, "It was pawned for 800 yuan."

After hearing the testimony, the judge ordered Cheng Xu to be brought to the dock. She was 44 years old.

The judge asked, "Why did you buy diamond rings from Yin and pawn them?"

She replied, "I took the diamond rings to Bao Cheng Silver Shop to exchange for money, but I didn't expect the owner, Cao Junqing, to detain them. I had previously owed Cao Junqing 800 yuan, so the money from Yin Cunfu's house could not be delivered. However, this matter has nothing to do with my daughter, Cheng Meifang. I am willing to repay the debt and request leniency."

Finally, Kuang Cheng Meifang testified that she was 18 years old and lived at No. 88 Hejia Lane, Shangwen Road. She did not go to Yin's house with her mother. She claimed that at that time, her husband was recuperating in Hangzhou, so she was taking care of him in Hangzhou. If the court did not believe her, she had a hospital certificate to prove it.

The judge examined the certificate and then invited prosecutor Wu Deying to the court to present his arguments.

After a long debate, the plaintiff's private prosecution agent lawyer requested to pursue the private prosecution portion, stating that 1,000 yuan had been received for the first diamond ring worth 1,600 yuan, leaving 600 yuan unpaid. The pawn ticket for the second diamond ring had been recovered, and the pawn amount was 800 yuan, plus 100 yuan in interest, totaling 900 yuan. Adding the previous 600 yuan owed, the total amount to be recovered was 1,500 yuan. He requested that Cheng Xu and Kuang Cheng Meifang be jointly responsible for the payment.

After hearing the testimony, the judge considered the case to be clear and declared the hearing closed. The verdict was scheduled to be announced at 4 p.m. on the 28th of this month. Cheng Xu was returned to custody, and Kuang Cheng Meifang was ordered to provide a reliable shop as surety for 1,500 yuan. Without surety, she would be taken into custody.

Observations on Foreign Banks Raising Interest Rates and Increasing the Issuance of Banknotes

China News Agency reports that foreign banks in Shanghai are recently issuing large amounts of banknotes and raising interest rates to absorb Chinese silver in order to absorb Chinese silver. A reporter from China News Agency interviewed Lin Kanghou, secretary of the Shanghai Banking Association, and economic expert Li Quanshi to find out the truth. The details are recorded below:

Lin's Opinion: According to Lin, the issuance of banknotes by foreign banks in China is a major loss of our country's financial sovereignty. It was only after the successive establishment of the China Traffic and Communications Banks that the Chinese people had great confidence in domestic banknotes. This is because the issuing Chinese banks have their ten percent reserve funds supervised and managed by the government. As for the issuance of banknotes by foreign banks in China, the amount was the largest during Yuan Shikai's era. In recent years, the Chinese people have used their own funds to provide foreign investment for enterprises, which is deeply unjust. As for Chinese banks, they hope that the government will handle this matter properly.

Li's Remarks: According to economic expert Dr. Li Quanshi, foreign banks want to issue a large number of banknotes and increase interest rates to absorb Chinese silver. The only effective way to increase the issuance of banknotes is to immediately exchange all foreign bank banknotes for cash, whether they are in the hands of the public or Chinese banks. As for foreign banks increasing interest rates to absorb Chinese silver, it is due to the recent awakening of the Chinese people. Recently, foreign banks have been shipping silver out of the country, and their reserves have been sharply reduced. Depositors are withdrawing their funds one after another. During the warlord era, some Chinese people even voluntarily deposited their funds in foreign banks without receiving interest. Now, the increase in interest rates is clearly a prelude to the decline caused by the sharp decline in depositors.

Foreign Interpretation: New Voice News Agency reports that the case of foreign banks increasing the issuance of banknotes and raising interest rates has attracted much attention. A reporter from New Voice News Agency learned from foreign banking circles that before the final accounts of 1934, British banks such as HSBC and Mercantile Bank, in view of the tight money supply in Shanghai, reissued the banknotes that had been gradually collected. After the final accounts, Chinese money shops, etc., because of the issuance of banknotes from China Traffic and Communications Banks, etc., immediately exchanged the foreign bank banknotes they received the next day. Moreover, the Chinese people welcomed the use of Chinese bank banknotes, so now, in view of the impropriety of the method, they have gradually withdrawn them. As for the increase in interest rates for depositors, it is due to price factors. Last year, the annual interest rate for depositors was about 1.75%. This year, the annual interest rate for HSBC, Mercantile Bank, and other three banks has been changed to 5%. As for the rumors that the Shanghai Banking Association has firmly requested a ban, according to Lin Kanghou, Secretary-General of the Association, there is no such thing.

Salvation Army Shanghai Branch to Launch Fundraising Campaign

Starting on March 1st, Goal is 30,000 Yuan

To Support Social Welfare Undertakings

The Salvation Army Shanghai Branch has decided to launch a fundraising campaign starting on March 1st, with a goal of 30,000 yuan to support various social and charitable works. The name of the Salvation Army is not yet familiar to the Chinese people, who think that it only helps foreigners. In fact, it takes care of both Chinese and foreigners, and in places like Beijing and Shenyang, it serves the Chinese people completely. In Shanghai, the Released Prisoners' Aid Society on Huade Road was founded by the Army and has achieved remarkable results. The majority of those it helps are Chinese. The Huade Road Prison is the largest in the world. Last year, Salvation Army officers received 11,200 released prisoners, about one-tenth of whom were given relief by the Army, such as clothing, medicine, food, and assistance to return to their hometowns. Last year, 499 Chinese released prisoners were assisted in returning to their hometowns, and 140 of them were helped by the Salvation Army to find work. As for foreign released prisoners who received assistance, there were 44 throughout the year. Sometimes the families of the prisoners are also assisted by the Association.

The Salvation Army has been in China for 18 years. It started with only six people in Beijing. Today, the entire army has reached 263 people, most of whom are Chinese. There are 90 meeting places throughout the country. Donations can be sent to the Army Headquarters at No. 422 North Suzhou Road.

Agricultural and Commercial Bank Orders Printing of New Banknotes

Central News Agency, Nanjing, 26th: The Agricultural and Commercial Bank, because most of the banknotes it has issued are old and damaged, has specially submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance to order the printing of new banknotes and to increase the amount of issuance. The Ministry of Finance has approved the ordering of 20 million yuan of new banknotes and has also approved an increase in the issuance amount of 2 million yuan.

General Overview of the Drought Disaster Relief Efforts in Various Provinces

Cheng Jingsheng's Report After Inspecting and Returning to Shanghai

Cheng Jingsheng, the executive director of the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Disaster Relief in Various Provinces, along with inspector Qiao Baoyuan and others, inspected disaster relief efforts in various counties of Jiangsu. He returned to Shanghai yesterday and reported that the disaster situation in Liyang, Lishui, Gaochun, and other counties is extremely severe. In the disaster areas they visited, many able-bodied men had fled to other places, leaving behind the elderly, weak, and disabled in desolate rooms, sighing to each other. Upon inspection of the houses, not only were there no savings, but the bottom of the cooking pots were covered in dust. When asked, they burst into tears. In Liyang County alone, no fewer than several thousand people have been sold as children to Wuxi and Shanghai. Young girls are sold for a mere three or five yuan. In Jiangpu, many have committed suicide due to hunger. Old women in Jurong, unable to bear the hunger, have resorted to running onto the road, hoping to be crushed by cars. The food of the disaster victims consists mostly of powdered weathered stone (commonly known as Guanyin powder), powdered elm bark, and buckwheat husks. In Gaochun and Lishui, many have died from intestinal blockages caused by eating weathered stone, and from poisoning caused by eating elm bark with sugar. In other counties, such as Jintan, filling their stomachs with bran and grass roots is considered a delicacy. Such a severe disaster is unprecedented in Jiangnan in recent decades. With three months to go before the wheat harvest, it will be difficult to survive without spring relief. It is reported that Zhang Lanping and Li Tianzhen, the directors of the association's Jiangsu inspection and distribution efforts, have appointed dedicated officials in each county. However, the disaster is so severe that the relief funds are insufficient, making it like a drop in the bucket, unlikely to provide a thorough rescue. According to Cheng's inspection, Liyang is classified as a particularly severely affected area, Lishui, Gaochun, and Jiangpu as the most severely affected areas, Jurong, Jintan, and Yixing as severely affected areas, and Zhenjiang, Jiangning, and Danyang as moderately affected areas. The inspection and distribution directors have already received 100,000 yuan in relief funds from the association (including funds allocated by the Central Winter Emergency Relief Committee). They are cooperating with the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, the World Red Swastika Society, the Chinese Jisheng Society, the Chinese Morality Society, the Catholic Action Society of China, and local charities in each county, working together to supplement each other's efforts and pool resources. It is estimated that the association has allocated 3,000 yuan to Liyang, with other groups providing over 90,000 yuan; 20,000 yuan to Lishui, with other charities providing over 3,000 yuan; 14,672 yuan to Gaochun, with other charities and the county magistrate raising 8.3 million yuan themselves (the county government has allocated temporary emergency relief separately); 3,000 yuan to Jiangpu, with other charities providing 3,600 yuan, plus 600 bags of flour; 4,000 yuan to Jurong, with other charities providing 21,000 yuan; 6,000 yuan to Jintan, with other charities providing 16,000 yuan; 3,000 yuan to Yixing, with other charities providing 20,000 yuan, plus 3,500 bags of flour; 2,440 bags of flour to Zhenjiang, equivalent to approximately 6,000 yuan (the Zhenjiang local drought relief committee is providing relief separately); 13,000 yuan to Jiangning, with other charities providing over 5,500 yuan, plus over 5,000 yuan already spent on porridge (the Jiangning local drought relief committee is providing over 1,400 shi of rice separately); 5,000 yuan to Danyang, with other charities providing 16,000 yuan, and the county relief branch providing 15,000 yuan. The remaining funds are being planned by Director Zhang and others. Except for Gaochun, where cash is distributed due to transportation difficulties, the above relief funds are used to purchase rice and flour, which are distributed based on household surveys and ticket allocation, prioritizing those in greatest need. As for work relief, the provincial government's construction department has a large-scale project in each county. The Chinese and Foreign Relief Association has also sent personnel to Lishui, Gaochun, and Jiangpu to carry out work relief.

Resolution of Competition Between Shanghai and Wuxi Freight Lines

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, in recent years, rural areas in the interior have gone bankrupt, and all industries are extremely depressed, especially the shipping industry. Therefore, the Shanghai-Wuxi freight lines in this city, such as Gongmao Shipping Bureau, Taichang Huiji Shipping Bureau, and Xiexing Shipping and Transportation Company, considering the unprofitable business of competition among the same industry, jointly established the Shanghai-Wuxi Shipping Joint Company in April last year to seek unity. However, when the Gongmao Shipping Bureau was established, the Wuxi Zhonghua Hengyu Shipping Company (which operates on the Wuxi-Liyang route) also simultaneously established the Shanghai-Wuxi freight line. Although the Gongmao Shipping Bureau repeatedly requested the Shanghai Inland River Shipping Trade Association to argue reasonably, the competent authorities perfunctorily shirked their responsibilities, leading to fierce competition between the two parties. Until the end of last year, the authorities of Zhonghua Hengyu Company also felt the difficulty of operating and believed that fighting each other would only lead to mutual losses. Therefore, through the mediation of Zhang Fengshou, the chief supervisor of the Shanghai Inland River Shipping Trade Association, Zhonghua Hengyu Company decided to lease the business rights to the Shanghai-Wuxi Shipping Joint Company, which was jointly established by the three bureaus, for a temporary period of three years. It is reported that the lease contract has been signed and the handover has been completed in recent days. The open and secret competition between the Shanghai-Wuxi freight lines in recent months has come to an end, which is a dawn for the future of inland river shipping.

Record of a Fallen Power Line on Min'guo Road

A Minor Worker Narrowly Escapes Death

Yesterday morning (the 26th) at 8:45, a trolley car No. 14 of the Chinese-owned Second Road, while driving north from Laoximen to Nanyang Bridge, for some unknown reason, the trailer bell at the rear of the car suddenly malfunctioned. The power line at that location was then seen to sag, resulting in an interruption of the current and preventing the car from proceeding. As a result, trolley cars on all north-south routes passing through the Chinese concession were immediately affected, stopping midway and forming a long, snake-like line. At that time, two shop assistants from a certain store were pulling and pushing a cart loaded with three large wooden boxes of goods, proceeding along the east side of the road. When they reached the spot, they suddenly heard a loud noise, sparks flew, and the triangular cement pole on the left-hand sidewalk broke at its base and fell horizontally, landing directly on top of the cart. The two shop assistants were startled and fell to the ground. The cart was immediately crushed, tilted, and cracked. Fortunately, the shop assistants had taken a step forward, and the pole did not fall on them, so they were unharmed. This was indeed very fortunate; otherwise, even if there was no danger of electric shock, the pole would have fallen on their heads and they would have been unable to withstand it. The shock of the electricity was so extreme that passersby could not help but rejoice. Afterwards, the police on duty reported the incident to their respective stations, and the trolley car company immediately ordered workers to repair the power lines and replace the pole, and traffic was restored. It is reported that there have been three instances of power lines breaking and falling in the Laoximen area recently, but none as dangerous as this one. During the dangerous situation, the one-way traffic regulation at that location should have been immediately suspended and temporarily put on alert, but the police there still allowed other vehicles to pass, seemingly without taking any measures to stop them. This is deeply regrettable. Although a tragedy has been avoided, it is a great fortune for society. However, the relevant authorities should pay attention to this.

Yesterday afternoon at around 3:00 PM, a lost boy of about ten years old was spotted on Rue Robert in western Shanghai by a police officer, who took him to the sub-station and then transferred him to the Caojiadu branch bureau. Donations for Zheng Shichao's Family Awaiting Collection

Funds Stored at the Ningbo Daily on Xizang Road

Zheng Shichao, a native of Ningbo, was working as a second officer on the Huamao ship of Renji Huaxin Company in this city. On New Year's Eve last year, Zheng fell into the cabin while working on the ship and died tragically, leaving behind his elderly mother in her seventies, as well as orphans and a widow, a family of seven, whose livelihood was cut off, a tragic and unbearable situation. Some time ago, the Shanghai Ningbo Daily published the details of the incident, and Zhou Ziqing and other enthusiastic fellow villagers saw it and took pity, remitting donations and instructing the newspaper to forward them to Zheng's family. Zheng's family originally lived at Lane 286, Rue Lafayette in the French Concession of this city, but recently moved elsewhere due to financial difficulties. Therefore, the funds cannot be forwarded. They are currently stored in the accounting department of the newspaper. Anyone who knows Zheng Shichao's family is requested to notify them immediately to collect the funds at the Fellow Villagers Service Department of the Shanghai Ningbo Daily in Pingle Lane, Xizang Road.

The Fourth Issue of the Popular Culture Bi-Monthly is Published

Since its publication, the Popular Culture Bi-Monthly has seen a surge in sales and subscriptions both locally and in other cities. At the same time, the publication has gradually reformed and enriched its layout and content. It is reported that the fourth issue has been published today. The contents include articles in the political and economic section such as Jiang Jiesheng's "London Anglo-French Agreement," Shen Zhiyuan's "A Review of the Pound Currency Policy in the Past Year," and Wu Qingyou's "The Indian Constitution Issue." The science and engineering section includes articles such as "The Standards and Names of Weights and Measures," "The Study of Color," "Positrons and Neutrons," "Two Optical Illusions," "New Words in Science and Engineering," "Think About It First," and "Small Research Topics," with attached illustrations. The interest in this issue is particularly strong compared to the previous issues. The retail price of this issue is six cents per copy, and the annual subscription price is one yuan and two jiao.

Nanjing Branch of the Two Railway Workers' Union Established

Since the establishment of the reorganization office of the Jinghu and Huhangyong Railway Workers' Union, the reorganization work has progressed rapidly. The preparatory work for the eleven branches along the entire line is largely complete. The Nanjing branch held a representative conference at the Nanjing Workers' School of the Ministry of Railways at 5:00 PM on the 24th. Forty-nine representatives, including Su Hanqing, attended. More than eighty people, including Yang Youren, the instructor of the special party branch, Di Chao, the representative of the Workers' Union reorganization office, and guests Zhang Rongchun and Huang Jingjian, attended. The presidium, composed of Yang Yuting, Li Youheng, and Li Deli, conducted the proceedings. Afterwards, Yang Yuting and Li Youheng reported on the purpose of the meeting and the preparation process. The party branch and Workers' Union instructors then gave speeches, detailing the significance of reorganizing the Workers' Union, the need to improve the organization in the future, strengthen training, and develop the direction of the business. Then, the branch officers were elected. As a result of the ballot count, Li Youheng, Li Deming, and Gan Asan were elected as officers, and Su Hanqing and Yang Yuting were elected as alternate officers. They were sworn into office on the spot. Afterwards, guests delivered speeches, and the officers gave replies. The meeting adjourned with a group photo at 8:00 PM.

Letter

To the editor:

We have examined the report in the local news section of your newspaper dated February 25, regarding the meeting of the Fifteenth District Branch of the Special Zone City Federation. The fourth item is clearly inconsistent with the facts. Although our association was introduced by Wan Xuanqing, an executive committee member of our association, to discuss jointly renting premises with the Fifteenth District Branch in January of last year, Zhu Zhichun of the branch did not seek our association's consent regarding the joint rental procedures, and instead acted independently, with the aim of benefiting himself, resulting in no contract being signed to date. Furthermore, according to him, the landlord suddenly increased the rent by 25% one month into the lease and signed a lease contract with the China Business Company, which manages the property. Furthermore, Zhu Zhichun acted personally on behalf of Renci Primary School, with various fraudulent acts that are difficult to describe in detail. Our association is currently negotiating based on reason. The report is clearly a one-sided promotion by the branch. In view of the inconsistency of the report, we would like to request a correction. Sincerely, Shanghai Inland River Shipping Trade Association, February 26.
