Shen Bao Local Supplement

Essays

Listen to Lytton's Tune

— Fang Yin

After the September 18th Incident, Lord Lytton, bearing the responsibility of resolving the "Manchurian Problem," made a trip to the Far East. Subsequently, he returned to Geneva and published the so-called "Lytton Report," aimed at "maintaining peace in East Asia." Afterward, news about him gradually diminished in newspapers.

In the investigation report, Lytton advocated that Manchuria should be jointly managed internationally, not exclusively by Japan. Naturally, Japan would not agree to this proposal. Who would willingly give up the fat they had already tasted? Even a three-year-old would know that this was futile. Consequently, Lord Lytton faced a rebuff in Geneva, and Japan withdrew from the League of Nations under the principle of "non-recognition of Manchukuo" by various countries.

Recently, Lytton reiterated his views on the Manchurian problem in the United States. In fact, these views remain the same old tune as those in the investigation report three years ago: still "requesting Japan's cooperation" and encouraging everyone (imperialists) to "jointly develop Manchuria."

Of course, under the principle of not harming Japan's interests in Manchuria, Japan welcomes investment from various countries. Even Lytton acknowledges that "Japan should be given considerable understanding regarding its handling of the Manchurian Incident" This so-called understanding naturally refers to Japan's special position in Manchuria. Japan's special position in Manchuria is precisely due to the creation of the puppet "Manchukuo" through military force.

"Lytton continued, stating that the League of Nations' handling of the Manchurian Incident was not a failure because the League's policy was primarily criticism, not the use of military force to enforce its beliefs" (Eleventh Washington National News dispatch). In fact, the League of Nations' reputation was long tarnished by Japan. Lytton's talk of success or failure is pointless. What pretense can still be salvaged? "Finally, Mr. Lytton believed that although Japan could develop Manchuria through peaceful means, Japanese troops must be withdrawn to maintain the goodwill of all countries in the world" (Eleventh Washington National News dispatch). Lytton's hope for Japan to withdraw troops is certainly unrealistic, but Lytton is not a fool and knows that Japan will not withdraw its troops. However, on the international stage, the tune must be loud enough to garner sympathy. In reality, they have other intentions. Haven't recent reports revealed that Britain will send a commercial delegation to Manchuria?

Old Man Fu

— Lini

Old Man Fu's departure and the arrival of a strange middle-aged woman at his small, humble earthen house, panting like an overworked ox and sobbing softly leaning against the doorway, spread throughout the village. It aroused the curiosity of all the women in the village and the malicious glee of the children, who all gathered at his door to watch the spectacle, surrounding the small earthen house.

Old Man Fu had a limp in his right leg, and his left shoulder swayed back and forth as he walked. It was said that he got this limp when he was young and got into trouble for stealing a woman. He—around forty years old—had a small, rotten pumpkin-like head with most of his hair gone, leaving a bald spot on top that looked like a flat piece of wax stone. His thin, triangular face had a pair of weasel eyes and thick, dark lips with a few gray cat whiskers on his upper lip. Although his appearance wasn't particularly handsome, his lips always wore a friendly smile, regardless of whether it was winter or summer, which made people feel close to him.

Ever since Old Man Fu had come to the village, the village's celebrations and funerals had been entrusted to him. Today he would be asked by someone to pick up the bride's sedan chair, tomorrow someone else would ask him to report a death to relatives. These had become Old Man Fu's specialty. At the same time, he was particularly more experienced and thorough than others in these matters. Therefore, the village people couldn't do without Old Man Fu whenever something happened.

A few years ago, when Old Man Fu was still young, the people in the village seemed to be richer than they were now, and they were particularly willing to spend money and make a grand display of their celebrations and funerals! They would invite guests for at least ten or eight days, making so much noise that even the chickens and dogs in the house wouldn't be at peace. This meant that Old Man Fu didn't have to cook for himself at home. He was called to help out and received five cents a day, plus a lot of "extras" and "grease" from the guests. His pockets were filled, and his two weasel eyes smiled even more narrowly.

Old Man Fu had no other hobbies except for drinking a cup or two of "white liquor" every day. Even women, whom he had loved when he was young, now seemed to disgust him. Since he drifted into the village, his attitude had become very proper and serious, and he had never caused any trouble over women. Because of his shrewdness and diligence, he had saved some money over the years and lent it to people in the village who were starting small businesses, earning a little interest each year.

After he finished his work during the day, he would drink his "white liquor" and, with a bit of a buzz, slowly drag his half-worn silk shoes, which were given to him by someone he had helped, and leisurely go to the stone steps in front of the ancestral hall to cool off and watch the evening clouds in the sky. At this time, those on the steps who were about the same age as him would always say to him in a half-serious, half-joking tone!

"Old Fu, why don't you find a woman? Are you going to live like a monk your whole life?"

"Women... disgusting things!" He would look at the sky, roll his weasel eyes full of red veins, and then close his eyelids tightly. "It's so clean like this, wo...men!" His voice was too slow, with a sense of regret, as heavy as lead.

"Haven't you already had a woman before?" Those people seemed to be deliberately probing into his origins.

"Why is the weather so stuffy! If the heavens don't send rain, it's really going to suffocate people." Old Man Fu would change the subject, and so, cleverly, their topic would turn to the weather.

The news of Old Man Fu's sudden departure and the arrival of a middle-aged woman sobbing softly in his small earthen house caused a stir in the peaceful village, with everyone making mysterious speculations.

Hanging

— Rui Zhi

"Zhou Ruisheng's grandmother hanged herself at home last night."

This news spread throughout the village early in the morning. Then all kinds of discussions spread through the streets and alleys of the village.

"Zhou Ruisheng has three brothers, and they still let their old mother hang herself."

"In these times, it's better to be dead than alive and suffering. Dying is cleaner."

"It's like a plague. Since the new year began, a lot of people have died in this village. Starvation, freezing, drowning, hanging, everything is happening."

"The heavens are blind. In this bad year, how can people survive?"

These kinds of discussions were heard everywhere in the alleys. Some were scolding Zhou's three brothers for being unfilial, not even being able to support an old mother. Some were cursing the heavens and the ghosts, saying they didn't protect living beings. But there were also some who knew that it was the bad year that caused it, or that it was a fate determined by heaven. And there were even some who were used to it and didn't think it was a big deal. In short, everyone had an opinion, whether right or wrong, and everyone was discussing it. The usually quiet village was stirred up by Zhou's family's affair.

Cheng Laobo from the Cheng Family Ancestral Hall was awakened by the Zhou family's death early in the morning. Listening to the mixed discussions of the women in the alley, he became impatient. After eating a bowl of very thin porridge, he went out alone.

Cheng Laobo was over seventy years old, and there were only a few people in the village who were about his age. So he knew everything about the village, who was good, who was bad, which family was doing well, which family was poor. He knew all these things in detail. As for the good and bad years, and the number of deaths in the village, he had seen a lot and was almost tired of it. But a bad year like last year, with people dying one after another, was the first time he had seen it in all his years.

Walking on the road, the voices of the conversations at the alleyway still pierced his ears sharply. Although he found the people who were talking annoying, he could only walk along silently. His feet were walking, but his mind was thinking:

"Damn it, these young people and girls, what are they talking about, death after death? They can't explain anything, but they have to talk to death. What business is it of theirs that someone's old woman died, just making a fuss. In these times, what does it matter if someone dies, even if ten more die, it's the same thing."

The more he thought about it, the more unhappy he became, and the voices of the conversations by the roadside seemed even sharper. He finally made it out of the village gate.

The fields outside the village gate were silent, with only the dry leaves and branches under the trees rustling a little in the wind. Cheng Laobo stood on the ridge at this time, the sun shining on his face, and the wind blowing his white beard. He felt a natural comfort in his heart. He looked at the vast fields in front of him, with the soil plowed loosely, and he guessed that this year's harvest would be good.

He stroked his face, twirled his beard, and a smile appeared on his face as he walked back and forth on the ridge. Thoughts flooded his mind one after another. He thought:

"This year's harvest should be better, right? I've lived this long, and I've never seen such a famine as last year, with so many people starving to death, freezing to death, and committing suicide. Those young people always talk about death when they hear about it, without thinking about doing anything serious, really..."

As he thought, he looked at the endless field of soil that had been plowed loosely, and his mind turned. He frowned and muttered to himself:

"Huh! The fields that were plowed last year weren't as loose as this!? But..."

His heart sank, and he couldn't help but think of Zhou Ruisheng's grandmother's suicide.

All Livelihood

— Yi An

Fond Memories of Old Dreams

— Simon

Over there, at the end of the sea, under the green coconut trees of the South Island, once were imprinted my pale, traceless, light dreams, the lingering, hesitant silver traces of love. In my dreams, I deeply savored the passion of flower-like, fragrant, tender blood-red lips! Lying quietly among the shadows of the leaves, I listened to the gentle melodies that young girls sang, melodies that flowed like the wind through their youthful voices. The young girls had captivating eyes that gave me beautiful, dream-like fantasies. Their eyes brewed poetic secrets of maidenhood, often immersing me in a blissful, forgetful state. But because of the heavy gift of love, I worried that I didn't have the capacity to bear it, and instead, I felt an inexplicable anxiety and melancholy.

The dream eventually fell like a star that twinkles once and then plummets from the sky. The beautiful dream has turned into black smoke, into shattered fragments of scattered fallen leaves. Now, in the grim recollection, I silently pick up the faded and broken remnants of the past, but they can no longer offer me any comfort. It is like stabbing a wounded heart with another sudden knife. Beyond that, I can only endure immense sorrow, watching helplessly as the last drops of youth's rich nectar flow away.

The strings of the zither are broken, the soft sounds are gone. What can I still see, what can I still hear? During the long days, my eyes are filled with misty tears. All happiness has been surrendered to the well of tears and sighs.

I originally wished that all the past would forever be thickly covered by the dust of time, never again having the heart to pursue it, lest I needlessly invite some embarrassing stings. But because my heart is not completely dead, how could I simply abandon the old dreams that once caused my life to tremble greatly and be deeply intoxicated? However, when I ignite the memory of the past, which seems both blurry and clear, I suddenly feel like I am losing consciousness. My body sways in mid-air like a kite with a broken string, completely scorched by the invisible flames of memory.

Knowing that the vanished joys cannot be pursued and the lost beautiful figures cannot be called back, just as fallen raindrops can never fly back to the sky. Yet, I stubbornly try to listen to the light singing of orioles and search for the colors of fresh green flowers in this deep autumn when the autumn wind has blown the flowers and leaves from the trees.

Where on this vast earth can I go to find my old dreams? The sky is so high and distant, the sea is so boundless, and the journey is so long and remote, like a misty, remote South Island dream! You, young girl, your feelings are truly as unpredictable as the weather at sea. It was so difficult for me to meet you, so much effort I used, but losing you was so easy. You quietly left without even looking back. Do you know that the person who was once so close to you all day long has become a wanderer in a foreign land? Although in the meantime, I have become indifferent to all the worldly splendor, the only thing I cannot become indifferent to is you. I still think of you every day! The impression you gave me was too profound. Although ruthless time has draped my life in gray robes, you always have a graceful and delicately beautiful face with a light smile, which is still clearly engraved in my heart, like a golden statue that cannot be destroyed. Therefore, I am mired in a prison from which I cannot escape. Now I am listlessly passing the years without joy or hope, staggering along the long road of wandering, singing the death knell of my own life. I don't feel a bit of regret, nor do I blame anyone. Everything that is worthy of boasting no longer belongs to me, just as the young girl already belongs to someone else. However, there will be a day when everything about you, young girl, will also not belong to you, and you will feel the loneliness of life.

But I bless you that you will not have such days. The sweet and painful souvenir you have given me is already a generous gift.

Wandering News

— Yafei

Our hometown is a solitary island standing amidst turbulent waves. It is surrounded by water, with no land routes for access. However, the water routes are only served by a few civilian boats.

There are beautiful scenery and famous historical sites. Emperor Qianlong visited the island during his tour of Jiangnan. Now, the Dragon Cave and Stone Elder Mountains, like the Lion Grove and Lingyan Mountain in Suzhou, are still forbidden from quarrying stones after his imperial decree, and the imperial inscriptions are still clearly visible on the stone walls. The lives of the villagers are very simple, and their customs are very honest and kind. Among the people who grew up on this solitary island, at least ninety-five out of a hundred have never left the province, and some have never even left the island. Since the Taiping Rebellion, this place has not suffered from war, and the villagers live in peace and contentment, considering it a paradise on earth. There are also very rich local products, but since the continuous natural disasters in recent years, this solitary island is not as prosperous as it once was!

On this solitary island, which is thousands of miles in circumference, people live scattered in groups of three or five families. Sometimes, there are only desolate wildernesses for ten or twenty miles, and no human habitation can be found. But sometimes, after walking only three or five steps, there is a village. Most people make a living by farming, but in recent years, many have gone to the docks to engage in commerce.

There are no postmen here. The post office hires a villager to deliver messages for ten yuan. This person who delivers letters is called the "Wandering News". Every morning, he carries a package and sends the letters he collected along the way the night before to the branch office (the so-called branch office is just a grocery store with a sign hanging in front of it that says "Agency for selling stamps", which is subsidized by the county post office). The letters are then transported to the county office by civilian boat. He then distributes the letters from the branch office. For each letter delivered, he receives six copper

Page 19

coins. Postcards and newspapers are half-price. This can be considered an extra expense for the recipient. However, in one respect, the sender can take advantage of a small benefit: letters sent within the island do not need to be stamped; he will deliver them himself and collect the porterage fee from the recipient.

For letters sent to distant places, he does not deliver them on the same day. He waits until he has several letters before delivering them together, so it is possible that a letter may take seven or eight days to be received.

He passes by our house, usually around seven o'clock in the morning, but in the afternoon it is only around dusk.

"Wandering News, how are you? Are you still delivering news?" When he delivered a letter this time I returned home, I couldn't help but ask him this.

"Yes, who would want to do this bitter job?" He says it's a bitter job, but in reality, there are many people who envy this bitter job!

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

Hollywood's Special Academy That Emphasizes Triple Education and Intellectual Instruction (Part 2)

— Zhujia Bo

If the reader suspects that teaching such young children to practice public speaking or recite poems is appropriate, Lucy Greer has an amazing record to show you. She can prove that first-grade students can recite more than 400 lines of poetry each year, and can devise and deliver their own speeches once a week. They do not have any problems with shyness or panic in front of a large audience. Furthermore, these children are extremely fond of going on stage to speak or recite in front of the public. This practice of memorization and public speaking is uninterrupted from first grade to ninth grade. Therefore, self-awareness, or mental uneasiness in front of the public, is virtually non-existent among trained Curtis students.

During the primary school period, Jimmy's lunch must be eaten at school. He can learn many good eating habits during the year. The school has food experts and doctors. After they have prepared Jimmy's menu, they make slight additions and subtractions to what everyone usually eats to suit the needs of each child. For example, when Jimmy ate lunch at school for the first time, he saw milk on his plate. He hated milk the most. He also saw vegetables, which he also hated the most. He felt very unhappy. But there was also a large roast leg of lamb, fruit, and a piece of cake on the plate. He only ate what he liked. He kept looking at his teacher, Lucy Greer. He was afraid she would condemn him, but she didn't pay any attention to him, which made him feel strange. He didn't have that kind of freedom at home.

But soon, he saw other children often going to the kitchen to ask for a second glass of milk. There were also children who were hungry during class and specially asked for leave to go get milk to drink. He felt that milk must be a good thing. So, unknowingly, he gradually began to drink milk. Eating vegetables was also a gradual process. Before they got used to eating vegetables, Lucy Greer made them eat juicy vegetable soups or salads, so that they would get the same vitamins A, B, and C. But according to Lucy Greer, ordinary children like to gnaw on radishes, celery, or eat spinach.

At the end of the first year, Jimmy could already say a few words in French and could swim back and forth in the pool. His sloping shoulders were also straightened, and the arches of his feet were gradually rising. His weight had also reached equilibrium. He had his body checked once a month and his mouth checked by a dentist every four months. By the fourth grade, he began to learn to box, had to be able to take a punch to the face without shedding a tear. He also practiced the 25-yard dash. He also learned the correct posture for playing tennis. He was no longer afraid of horses and liked riding. He also dared to lean back and jump into the water. He had also become an expert in social dancing. He could also somersault, do tiger jumps, or walk on his hands. He also learned water rescue work. In addition, baseball, football, etc. were all things that every male student should know.

There was also a drama class there, which every student liked to join. Charlie Chaplin's two sons, Charles and Sydney, and Lawrence Tibbett's two twins, Lawrence and Richard, were children endowed with performing talent.

If Jimmy had a sister, her physical training after entering school would be exactly the same as Jimmy's, except for boxing. But women, in addition to boxing, added a lot of flexibility work, stage dance, archery, and indoor basketball.

When Apricot entered the seventh or eighth grade, she had gradually become interested in literature or poetry. And, beyond his mother's expectations, he was able to appreciate Shakespeare. Fortunately, the professor who taught Jimmy Shakespeare was not a scholar who only took things out of context or specialized in textual research. After explaining it in simple and extremely precise language, he asked each student to play a role in the play. In this way, they gained a deeper understanding of Shakespeare's works!

Of course, the curriculum of the Curtis School includes everything that a middle school should have. Students graduating from Curtis School can directly enter the highest-level university. All the courses there, whether science or literature, are very profound and rigorous, although each student must choose a major that is close to his nature, such as botany, biology, or geology. For example, Jimmy is already in the ninth grade. He chose to major in geology, so that when he goes to university, he can directly enter the university's geology class. Or, if he does not go to university, he can also work as a geological surveyor in an oil mining company.

The above does not describe all the work of the Curtis School in creating a good citizen. The more important work of the Curtis School is to train children's politeness, self-control, and make them reliable and useful citizens. He must learn to respect the rights of others, be tolerant, and be able to get along with others. He has learned a skill to convince people in the nine years of public speaking practice, so that when they enter the world in the future, they will not be despised as a dandy who cannot distinguish between beans and wheat. (The End)

Joan Crawford Describes Her Ambition to Perform on Stage

— Xifu

Joan Crawford recently built a small theater in her Brentwood Heights residence, next to the swimming pool. The roof is white, and the walls are made of unpainted wooden boards, simple and chic. It carries a mysterious air, because although people are talking about it outside, no one has been inside. One of Joan's old classmates went to see it and asked her what it was for. Joan told her that she wanted to perform on stage there during her free time in between filming. The following are the reasons why she wants to perform on stage:

She said: "I can't be a movie star forever. To be worthy of myself, I must ask for development. I need a lot, and stage experience is one of them." Joan herself criticized herself and said: "I lack the ability to be confident. I don't have a peaceful attitude. I often feel sorry for myself. Often during screenings, I can't eat all day. By the time the movie is screened, I'm almost a wreck. I must find a way to correct this problem. I can only find a way from the stage. I'm not seeking fame, I want experience."

"But where does the time come from? According to my contract, I have to film three movies a year. The company has the right to ask me to film one more, for a total of four. One movie may take as long as five months to film. When the second movie starts, I have no prior notice. So, although I want to perform on stage, I don't have time to perform, and I don't have time to practice. Therefore, I can only practice and rehearse at home first. That is, during the free time between filming, gather a few close friends and rehearse plays at home." According to Joan, she likes to perform historical plays. Or the first play she rehearsed was "Joan of Arc."

"What else?" her friend asked. This question revealed Joan's even greater ambition. She not only wants to perform historical plays on stage, but also wants to perform operas. She practices singing for one hour every day. Her throat is extremely wide, with a range of three octaves. She has to practice her voice at six o'clock in the morning and at lunchtime. She said: "I will sing in the second movie. That's the first time in my life. Would you like to listen?" As she said that, she took out a few records and put them on the record player. Sure enough, the tone was melodious and pleasant, which surprised her old classmate.

Joan was originally an ambitious woman. What was she twelve years ago? What was she? Probably many people know, five or six years ago, she was just an ordinary dancer. But she is full of ambition and constantly trains herself. Now she is a very popular superstar. Since she has this ambition to perform on stage and even go to the opera house, who can stop her? She is only twenty-five or six years old now, and her future is still bright, so let's wait and see.

Film Novel

Loving Mother of Students (Grand Girl) (3)

— Shu Min

Niperton was a black man, his shiny black face and his eyes with more white than black, no longer the timid and pitiful little student he used to be. At that time, because his homework was not up to par, he was dragged by Miss Merrill to the principal's office, where he tearfully told Miss Bales that because his family was poor, he had to work at night to earn some money to supplement his family, so he abandoned his homework. Miss Bales felt sorry for him after hearing his words. She didn't have much money in the bank, but she signed a check for twenty-five yuan for him. She kept seventeen yuan and fifty cents for herself, thinking that she would be paid soon, so it didn't matter. Besides, she would have a pension in two years, which was her guarantee for old age, so she didn't worry about money.

She said to the three of them very kindly, "What can I do for you?" Ward stepped forward and said, "Miss Bales... we..." He paused, and then said quickly, "We're here to tell you that we're on your side, no matter what others say!" William Biden also said, "That's right, Miss Bales." Niperton also quickly said, "That's right, it must be so." The principal thanked them in his mouth, but he felt a pang of sadness in his heart, and grateful tears filled his eyes. She reached into her large bag for a handkerchief. She felt a handkerchief, and when she pulled it out, she didn't expect two dice to come out with it and fall on the table, making a seven. Those were Dade's dice, which she had grabbed from him when he and her students were gambling.

At this time, Niperton saw a seven and his eyes widened like copper bells, and he couldn't help but shout, "A natural!" Bales was surprised and said, "Niperton, what are you talking about?" Niperton pointed to the two dice and said, "A seven jumps out! I think there's something... I think..." As he said, he grabbed the two dice and threw them on the table, and couldn't help but exclaim, "Holy Jicoti! Another natural!" Bales asked, "What? Do you call seven a natural?" Niperton didn't answer her words, and carefully looked at the dice. After looking at it for a long time, he suddenly shouted, "Hey, this isn't just any dice! This is simply a calendar, with three hundred and sixty-five sevens on it. Look, left is seven, right is also seven. Miss Bales, where did you get it from? This is defective!"

Bales exclaimed in surprise, "Defective!" She glared angrily at Dade's direction outside the window, when suddenly she frowned and had an idea. She then said to her three students, "You two can go, leave Niperton here." She said to Niperton, "You stay here. I want to talk to you... talk about this shameful gambling that you know so well." As she spoke, she couldn't help but feel proud. After Ward and William nodded and left, Roulan Bales immediately turned around and said to Niperton, "Good Niperton Jones! Now you tell me everything you know about this terrible game!" She fiddled with the two dice while thinking.

It was another afternoon, and like a brave warrior going to the battlefield, Roulan Bales walked into Dade's place. In her large pocket was a check, her salary, totaling two hundred and fifty yuan. She had already learned all the methods and terms of throwing dice from Niperton. Roulan laughed to herself, "A good teacher can always get some knowledge from his students." At this time, it was almost dinnertime, and the place was still empty. Dade was surprised to see her come in and asked, "What are you doing here again?" Roulan Bales picked up a stool next to him, sat down, and smiled, "Nothing." She deliberately smelled Dade's dinner, praising its taste; Dade said he cooked it himself. As he spoke, Roulan deliberately corrected his grammatical errors from time to time. Dade then asked, "Hey, what are you here to do? Are you here to correct my grammar?" (To be continued)

Shen Bao Local Supplement Automobile Weekly

Reasons for Increased Gasoline Consumption While Driving

— Zhen Min

When buying a car, the first question that car owners are most concerned about is the gasoline consumption per mile. But how much gasoline is consumed per mile is really a difficult question to determine. Engineers from various countries have jointly studied this issue and conducted dozens of tests under various conditions, but have not been able to obtain definite results. However, the approximate factors of gasoline consumption are nothing more than the following: (A) the roughness of the road surface; (B) the type of fuel; (C) the number of passengers; (D) the softness of the tires; (E) the type of road surface; (F) the slope of the road surface.

The same car consumes 10% more gasoline per mile when driving on a rough road surface than when driving on a smooth road surface. Inferior fuel consumes more gasoline per mile than high-quality fuel, because the combustion heat (per unit) of this inferior gasoline is very weak. Although the price is cheap, the result is uneconomical. The test results show that driving with this inferior fuel increases the consumption per mile by 8%.

Vehicles with more passengers increase the weight of the entire vehicle, and the reaction from the ground also increases accordingly. In this way, a huge amount of horsepower is needed to push the car body. This huge horsepower cannot be achieved without a large amount of gasoline. According to the test results, for every ton of weight added to the car, the gasoline consumption per mile increases by 15%. This result is difficult to predict.

Under-inflated tires are enough to increase the resistance of the ground, and also increase the braking horsepower. Gasoline consumption increases accordingly. The exact number of this increased consumption has not yet been determined, because the air pressure inside the tires is constantly changing.

Driving on asphalt roads consumes very little gasoline per mile, but driving on concrete roads increases gasoline consumption by 12%, because the resistance increases. The consumption of driving on cinder roads and gravel roads increases even more, probably by 17%.

The slope of the road surface has the greatest impact on gasoline consumption. When driving uphill (over a bridge or up a slope), the gasoline consumption increases accordingly because a large amount of engine power is needed to propel the car body. For every 2% of height, gasoline consumption increases by 4%. When driving downhill, if the throttle is turned off and the car body is allowed to coast down, then gasoline can be saved by 3.6%. Therefore, the average gasoline consumption for driving uphill and downhill is just offset.

The speed is also closely related to gasoline consumption, but at the same time, the road conditions must also be taken into account. Although the speed increases when driving on a smooth road surface, the resistance of the tires on the road surface is reduced accordingly, and the power needed to propel the car body is reduced accordingly. The gasoline consumption per mile is naturally reduced a lot. Conversely, on rough roads, the increase in speed greatly increases resistance, and the gasoline consumption per mile increases very quickly.

The faster the speed, the greater the air resistance. This air resistance is enough to excessively consume the engine's power and increase gasoline consumption per mile. Although the bodies of new cars are extremely streamlined, they are still unavoidable from air resistance, so this gasoline consumption cannot be avoided, and it increases with speed.

In addition to the above-mentioned reasons, there is also a seemingly unimportant but actually important issue, which is the engine's resistance. The interior of the engine is mostly metal-to-metal contact and friction, and there is a great deal of resistance in this contact and friction. Therefore, when the engine is braking, part of the power (it can be said that a large part) is used to offset this resistance, and the remaining part of the power is used to propel the car body. Therefore, the greater the engine resistance, the greater the gasoline consumption per mile. Poorly designed cars often have this drawback. Better-designed cars have reduced gasoline consumption to a minimum due to improved lubrication, but there is no way to completely eliminate this resistance.

Now we can summarize that the reasons for the increase in gasoline per mile are (1) the roughness of the road surface; (2) the increase in air and engine resistance; (3) the increase in the slope of the road surface; (4) the weakness of the tires; (5) the saving of gasoline, etc.; (6) the increase in the weight of the car body.

Hudson and Terraplane, All Equipped with Steel Roofs

— Fu

Some say that 1935 must be one of the most important years in automobile history, because steel roofs were implemented and adopted in that year. It has been fifteen years since steel roofs were recognized as a goal by general engineers. From the appearance, it seems very simple and not of great significance, but in fact, after the steel roof is completed, several complex problems are completely resolved. As far as car owners are concerned, the adoption of steel roofs really makes the all-steel body stronger and safer. Passengers can sit safely in the all-steel car body, and at the same time, they can use the latest four-season ventilation system to enjoy extreme comfort. This ventilation device is also the latest progress in the automotive industry.

The Hudson Car Body Manufacturing Factory specializes in manufacturing various car bodies for Hudson and Terraplane car assembly. There are many engineering experts in the factory who have devoted themselves to studying the steel roof problem for many years. They all admit that the use of steel roofs not only makes the car body structure more solid, but also greatly contributes to the appearance and safety. However, the reason why it has not been implemented is because there are many obstacles. One of these obstacles is how to avoid the annoying sound that naturally occurs on the flat and wide diaphragm surface of the roof. Another problem is that the natural expansion and contraction of metals has a great impact on the car body structure, and it must be eliminated. Fortunately, these problems have now been solved, and all 1935 Hudson and Terraplane sedans can be equipped with steel roofs. The method of making the steel roof absolutely quiet is particularly ingenious. Some of the principles imitate the management of sound waves by radio engineers. A material is applied to the roof, so the annoying sound that naturally occurs on the roof is eliminated by mutual resistance. Furthermore, due to the adoption of this structure, the appearance of the car body is extremely magnificent and the solidness is taken to an extreme. The new car body and chassis have now become a true all-steel combination as a whole, completely unaffected by climate or expansion and contraction. The solidness of its construction has been universally recognized by the automotive engineering industry.

The Economic Performance of British Small Cars

— Yu

Hillman Minx Travels Over a Thousand Miles for Just Over Two Pounds

A reporter for the automobile column of the "Argus" newspaper in Melbourne, Australia, recently drove a 10-horsepower Hillman Minx sedan from Melbourne to Sydney to test the comfort and economy of light cars. The total distance was 1,150 miles, and the total cost of gasoline and other fuels was only two pounds and three shillings, averaging 23 miles per hour. The car carried three passengers and their luggage. This achievement is not easy.

The fuel consumption averaged 42 miles per gallon. The gasoline used was "Shell Imperial" brand, and the price per gallon ranged from one shilling and five pence to one shilling and eleven pence. It maintained its normal state throughout the entire journey, so in this 1,150-mile journey, each passenger only spent fourteen shillings and four pence.

The departure date was Thursday at 7:30 PM. The gasoline tank had six gallons of gasoline left, worth eight shillings and six pence. After starting the journey, there was a strong headwind. The car traveled along the Hume Highway and finally arrived at Albury shortly after midnight. The gasoline left in the tank was still more than half a gallon. Five gallons of gasoline were purchased in Albury, worth seven shillings and six pence. No other oil or water was needed. At this time, the journey was 200 miles, and the speed per hour reached 35 miles, but the engine was still relatively warm. To maintain the temperature of the radiator, a part of the engine cover was covered with kraft paper for the rest of the journey. After dinner, the journey continued. After crossing the border, the good stone pavement of Victoria was not lost. Then, the car traveled for several miles on a road under construction, which was rugged and uneven, and full of mud, which was very difficult to travel on. At dawn, the car passed Gundagai and had breakfast at Gekkin. By the time the car reached Yass, there was still fuel left in the tank. Two gallons of gasoline were purchased there, at a price of one shilling and eleven pence per gallon. Later, another gallon was purchased in Goulburn, worth one shilling and ten pence. One gallon was purchased in Picton, worth one shilling and ten pence. Lunch was at a hotel in Berrima, which has been open for a hundred years. Prime Minister Lyons sometimes stays there. The car arrived at its destination, Sydney, on Friday afternoon. There was still one gallon of gasoline left in the fuel tank. The cost of this journey from the departure point to Sydney averaged 33.8 miles per hour and cost one pound, three shillings and three pence.

Before starting the return journey on Saturday night, one pint of gasoline was purchased, worth one shilling. The gasoline shops purchased gasoline along the way were Goulburn, Albury, and Benalla. The car continued to travel that night and arrived in Melbourne on Sunday afternoon. There was wind along the way, and the average speed was reduced, at 30.26 miles per hour. Therefore, gasoline consumption was also less. The total fuel consumption was only twelve and a half gallons, worth eighteen shillings and nine pence, averaging 46 miles per gallon. During this test, the light car performed very well. During the operation of British light cars, there are often unexpectedly pleasant tremors, but this Hillman Minx was able to completely eliminate them. The comfort of driving was particularly satisfactory. When the car was driving, the occupants often slept for a long time and were not awakened by the movement of the car. This small four-cylinder, ten-horsepower engine was able to climb over several steep mountain paths without hindrance. When shifting gears, there was no need to move the clutch because of the freewheel device. It was also very smooth and pleasant when going downhill. The brakes and steering wheel were very good and easy to use. The Ross steering gear was particularly comfortable and pleasant. Therefore, after this test, it is more than enough to prove that British light cars are economical and suitable.

Recent Progress of Highways in Zhejiang Province

— Cheng Yuqing

In the past decade, only 1,400 kilometers were built; in the last twenty years, 3,100 kilometers were created.

In recent years, Zhejiang Province's construction achievements have been remarkable. Among them, highways are the most prominent. This fact is sufficient to prove it. Since the establishment of the Provincial Highway Bureau in the eleventh year of the Republic of China, highway construction began. However, due to financial constraints, the project was often suspended. Up to the twenty-first year, the total length of main and branch lines completed in ten years was only 1,400 kilometers. Since the twenty-second year, after Zeng Yangfu came to head the Construction Department, he recognized the rampant banditry, local unrest, decline of industry and commerce, and the plight of the rural areas. He urgently needed to build highways extensively to facilitate transportation in various places. He then drafted a highway outline plan and implemented it earnestly to remedy the situation. The plan was divided into nine major trunk lines and forty-six branch lines, totaling fifty-five lines with a total length of more than 4,800 kilometers. At the same time, he requested the National Economic Council to allocate road construction funds to supervise and expedite the construction of highways in seven provinces. The main and branch lines within Zhejiang Province were immediately surveyed and constructed day and night, proceeding actively. Over a period of two years, they were completed successively. The first phase completed included the Jinli and other eighteen roads, with a total length of more than 750 kilometers. The second phase completed included the Guan Zhou and other twenty-three roads, with a total length of more than 980 kilometers. As of the end of the twenty-third year, the total length of highways completed in the province was 3,100 kilometers. The various route sections are described separately as follows:

(1) Jinli Road: This road runs from Jinyun to Lishui. The mountain opening project was very large. Construction began in December of the twenty-first year and was completed and opened to traffic in April of the twenty-third year.

(2) Changkai Road: This road includes Changtong (Changshan to Tongcun), Tonghao (Tongcun to Haoling Pass), and Xiafeng (Xiakou to Fengling) sections, as well as the Baisha Pass branch line and Baoan Street branch line. Only the Changtong section was completed in the twenty-first year. It was not until the end of the twenty-second year that all sections were completed and connected to traffic.

(3) Changkai Section: From Huabu via Xingkou to Kaihua, construction began in April of the twenty-second year and was completed in November.

(4) Qiuping Road: This road runs from Caoping to Qiuchuan on the Changyu Road and is one of the border defense roads. It has already been completed.

(5) Scenic Area Branch Lines: The scenic areas of this province are connected to nearby highways by branch lines. The completed ones include the Fanyun branch line, the Lishui Sanyan Temple branch line, and the Nanmingshan branch line, to facilitate tourist visits.

(6) Yinjiang Bridge Branch Line: This branch line branches off from Hengzhang Bridge on the Yinfeng Road to Yinjiang Bridge, with a length of eight kilometers. It has been contracted for lease by the Yinfeng Motor Company and has been completed and opened to traffic.

(7) Yichang Road: The earthwork for the section of this road from Yiwu to Dongyang was constructed by local conscripted labor. The Jiangdong Gang Bridge is a large project and was contracted out by the Provincial Highway Bureau. It was completed in November of the twenty-second year and opened to traffic first. The route from Dongyang to Changle in Sheng County is longer and the project is more difficult, so it was not fully completed and connected to traffic until May of the twenty-third year.

(8) Caosheng Road: This road runs from Haoba to Shushutan in Sheng County. With the permission of the people's request, a branch line from Lin'ao to Zhangjiabu was added, and the connection lines of the Shenghang, Shengchang, Shengxin, and Shengsan Roads in Sheng County were also constructed to facilitate connection. Construction began in October of the twenty-first year and was completed at the end of February of the twenty-third year. It was also leased to the Haoxin Motor Company for operation.

(9) Fuxin Road: This road runs from Fuyang to Shangjiangkou in Xindeng, connecting to the Hangfu Road. Construction began in March of the twenty-second year and was completed at the end of May of the twenty-third year. The Provincial Highway Bureau is responsible for opening it to traffic.

(10) Tongjian Road: This road runs from Shangjiangkou in Tonglu to Yangcunshu in Jiande, separated by the Fen Shui River and connected to the Fuxin Road. Construction began in April of the twenty-second year and was completed in June of the twenty-third year. Currently, a ferry dock is temporarily set up at Yijiang. The Provincial Highway Bureau is preparing to open it to traffic.

(11) Jianshou Road: This road runs from Jiande County seat via Yangcun Bridge, Baisha Wharf to Shouchang. Construction began in March of the twenty-second year and was completed in May of the twenty-third year.

(12) Xiangxi Road: This road runs from Xiangshan to Xize Wharf and is a section of the national defense road in the Ningbo area. Construction began at the end of September of the twenty-second year. The roadbed and bridges have been completed, but only the dirt road is passable. The formal road surface will be paved after funds are raised.

(13) Jinlan Road: This road runs from Jinhua to Lanxi and was built to connect the Shouchu Road and the Jinwuyong Road. All projects, except for bridges and road surfaces, are handled by the county governments. Construction began in March of the twenty-third year and was completed in early September.

(14) Tianmu Mountain Road: This road runs from Zaoxi near Yuqian County to the foot of Tianmu Mountain and is a branch line of the Hanghui Road. Construction began on March 10 of this year. The earthwork is handled by the county government through conscripted labor. It was fully completed in October. The Provincial Highway Bureau opened it to traffic in November.

(15) Longpu Road: This road runs from Longquan in Zhejiang Province to Pucheng in Fujian Province and is an important border defense road. It is 51 kilometers within Zhejiang Province and 39 kilometers within Fujian Province, all of which are constructed by Zhejiang Province. It was declared completed at the end of October.

(16) Ningheng Road: This road runs from Ningbo to Hengshan, remotely connecting to Xiangxi Road across Xiangshan Port. The project is handled by the Yin County government and has been fully completed.

(17) Zhenluo Road: This road runs from Zhenhai to Luotuo Bridge. The section from Zhenhai to Wangjia utilizes the Zhen branch line Yilu. The funds were raised by Zhenhai County, and the project was handled by the Highway Bureau on its behalf and completed at the end of July.

(18) Xintian Road: This road runs from Sanxi Town in Xinchang via Bamao in Xinchang to Tiantai. All projects are contracted out by the Provincial Highway Bureau. Construction began in April of the twenty-second year and was completed in July of the twenty-third year. It is currently preparing to open to traffic.

(19) Tianlin Road: This road runs from Tiantai to Linhai. Construction began in November of the twenty-second year and was completed at the end of June of the twenty-third year. However, a small part of the project needs to be cleaned up before it can be opened to traffic.
